<a id="s13-6"></a>

## 13.6. Vehicles

There are three vehicles in the game, each having a specific purpose at the
time it is acquired. The following sections describe each vehicle in
detail, including properties both in and out of battle. The statistics
given for each vehicle are very roughly based on the character statistics,
but are intended more as a means of comparison between each vehicle rather
than with the individual party members. I hope to give more accurate values
for these statistics at a later date.

The vehicles cannot be sold.

<a id="s13-6-1"></a>

### 13.6.1. Land Rover

LAND-ROVER - 'Armored vehicle that can drive over quick sand.'


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

Place Acquired: Machine Centre, south of Krup

> **Time Available: After Demi joins the party**


```
|                              |              |
| SP:     740                  |  Statistics  |
|                              |              |
| Weapon: Rocket Launcher      | Attack : 200 |
|                              | Defence: 210 |
| Optin:  CLUSTER x8           | Agility: 50  |
|         GRAVITN x8           | Dextrty: 65  |
|                              |              |
```

The Land Rover is the first of the three vehicles acquired. Its primary
function is to allow the party to cross quicksand, although it can traverse
any open land in the game. It is a very useful means of transportation once
it has been acquired, as it can cover large distances quite quickly, and is
also easier to do battle with. It is not as powerful as the Ice Digger, and
probably won't be used at all after this new vehicle is acquired.

CLUSTER - This weapon launches a cluster grenade into the air, which
  ¯¯¯¯¯¯¯   explodes to create a spread of fire onto all enemies.
            A force-based weapon.

GRAVITN - This weapon launches a gravity field onto each enemy, pulling
  ¯¯¯¯¯¯¯   at them with powerful forces.
            A gravity-based weapon.

<a id="s13-6-2"></a>

> 🥉 **Glacier Grinder** — Use the Ice Digger for the first time. _(RetroAchievements · 3 pts)_


### 13.6.2. Ice Digger

ICE-DIGGER - 'Vehicle that can pass through walls of ice.'


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

Place Acquired: Spaceport, on Dezolis
Time Available: After first Dark Force is defeated


```
|                              |              |
| SP:     960                  |  Statistics  |
|                              |              |
| Weapon: Twin Lasers          | Attack : 230 |
|                              | Defence: 190 |
| Optin:  NAPALM  x8           | Agility: 35  |
|         N-SPHER x4           | Dextrty: 50  |
|                              |              |
```

The Ice Digger is the most powerful of the vehicles. Its primary function
is to allow the party to pummel through the ice walls on Dezolis, but it
can also cross quicksand like the Land Rover. It is just as fast as the
Land Rover, and is far more useful in battle. It has the most SP of all the
vehicles, and also inflicts the most damage. Even after acquiring the
Hydrofoil, you will probably want to use the Ice Digger for most travel.

NAPALM  - This weapon launches a spray of flammable liquid that is
  ¯¯¯¯¯¯    ingnited on release to form a spread of fire over all enemies.
            A fire-based weapon.

N-SPHER - This weapon launches a sphere of intensely electrified negative
  ¯¯¯¯¯¯¯   energy, that pulls all enemies to its core.
            The weapon kills all enemies instantly.

<a id="s13-6-3"></a>

> 🥉 **Hyper Hovercraft** — Use the HydroFoil for the first time. _(RetroAchievements · 3 pts)_


### 13.6.3. Hydrofoil

HYDROFOIL  - 'A hover craft that can be driven over oceans.'


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

Place Acquired: Spaceport, on Motavia
Time Available: After speaking to Dezolisian bishop


```
|                              |              |
| SP:     680                  |  Statistics  |
|                              |              |
| Weapon: Twin Plasma Cannons  | Attack : 170 |
|                              | Defence: 190 |
| Optin:  TH.GRID x8           | Agility: 65  |
|         X-BURST x2           | Dextrty: 80  |
|                              |              |
```

The Hydrofoil is the weakest of all three vehicles. Its primary function is
to allow the party to cross the water on Motavia, but it can also cross
land (including quicksand). It cannot dig through ice. It is about twice as
fast as the other vehicles, meaning it is the quickest mode of transport
other that teleportation. On the down side, the Hydrofoil is the least
useful in battle, taking more damage and dealing less. This, coupled with
its low SP, makes combat in the Hydrofoil a little risky. Unless traversing
water, it is best to use the Ice Digger.

TH.GRID - This weapon launches a super-charged lightning ball over the
  ¯¯¯¯¯¯¯   enemies, that then splits to form a cascade of thunder.
            An electric-based weapon.

X-BURST - This weapon launches a beam of pure energy that sends out a
  ¯¯¯¯¯¯¯   high-intensity shockwave upon impact, hitting all enemies.
            A radiation-based weapon.

<a id="s13-7"></a>

## 13.7. Special

This section contains all the items that cannot be used or equipped from
any menu, but may have some other purpose. None of these items can be
bought or sold, and they are all essential to the story. They will either
be lost after they have fulfilled their purpose, or will remain in the
inventory until the end of the game.

ALSHLINE   - 'Medicine that turned stone back to flesh.'


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

Acquired in Warehouse Basement.

If the party enter Zema while carrying ALSHLINE, the villagers
             will return from stone statues to their normal state. The
             ALSHLINE is lost after this event has taken place.

CONTROLKEY - 'The system start up key for the Machine Center.'


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

Acquired in Machine Centre.

The CONTROLKEY is an entirely pointless item that must be
             acquired in order to get the Land Rover. It is lost after the
             Land Rover is obtained.

CANCELLER  - 'All-purpose sensor with stealth capabilities.'


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

Acquired on Zelan.

The artificial satellite Kuran is originally in Stealth Mode,
             meaning it is undetectable to radar. Returning to the Landale
             while having the CANCELLER in your possession causes Kuran to
             become visible. The CANCELLER is lost after defeating Dark
             Force on Kuran.

ECLPSTORCH - 'Nothing is known about this weapon.'


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

Acquired in Air Castle Basement.

When the party approaches the Carnivorous Trees while carrying
             the ECLPSTORCH, the forest is burned to ashes. The ECLPSTORCH
             will stay in the inventory until the party return to Gumbious
             Temple, where it will be given back to the Dezolisians.
             This item can be used in battle as the ST. FIRE Skill, but as
             it is neither expendable nor equipment, the ECLPSTORCH cannot
             be categorized as anything but special.

AERO-PRISM - 'Nothing is known about this weapon.'


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

Acquired in Soldiers' Temple.

The AERO-PRISM generates a powerful beam of light that points
             directly at Rykros, after being taken out of Soldiers' Temple.
             It also removes Rykros' veil of invisibility once the party
             are close enough. It stays in the inventory until the end.

RYKR-RING  - 'Nothing is known about this item.'


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

Acquired in Courage Tower.

One of the Rings of the Stars, the RYKR-RING is not included
             in the Head Protection section above because it can't be worn.
             It is essential, however, to prove to Le Roof that his trials
             have been completed. It stays in the inventory until the end.

The PSYCO-WAND, PALMA-RING, MOTA-RING, DEZO-RING, ALGO-RING and ELSYDEON
are also special, essential items, but they are covered in the relevant
equipment sections above.
14. Enemies                                                           CENMS

<a id="s14"></a>

# 14. Enemies

A sizeable part of the game will be spent in battle. This section is
designed to provide information on every biomonster, machine, darkspawn,
and evil being that you may have to face. The first two sections provide
lists of creatures by their location and their type. The last section gives
a complete alpabetical list of every enemy in the game, along with their
statistics and additional notes.

<a id="s14-2"></a>

## 14.2. By Type

<a id="s14-2-1"></a>

### 14.2.1. Biomonsters

Biomonsters are hostile creatures that are the product of genetic mutation,
unusual environmental conditions and the presence of the Darkness. They are
varied in their appearance and nature, but all share similar properties.
They are mostly susceptible to certain status effects and elemental damage,
although certain biomonsters will have different weaknesses and resistances
to some elements. Most biomonsters are encountered while outside or in the
earlier dungeons.
Falgues           - Xanafalgue
                    Gicefalgue
Zoran Bult        - Zoran Bult
Novas             - Igglanova   (Boss)
                    Guilgenova
Crawl Insects     - Crawler
                    Carrion Cr
                    Caterpillr

                    InfantWorm  (1)
                    InfantWorm  (2)
                    Snow Worm

                    Forced Fly
                    Helex

                    FlyScreamr
                    Tech-Plant

                    Elmelew

<a id="s14-2-2"></a>

### 14.2.2. Machines

Machines are the remnants of the old world before the 'Great Collapse'.
They vary in their design and function, but all have the same purpose - to
destroy. They are immune to most standard status abnormalities, but may
suffer similar effects from other means. They are usually quite resistant
to some elemental damage, and this may stretch into immunity in some cases.
Most machines are encountered in hi-tech dungeons.
Drones            - Arm Drone
                    Sat.Minion
                    Star Drone
Bits              - Sensor Bit
                    Gunner Bit
                    ProtectBit
Sentries          - Neowhistle
                    Seeker
                    Sweeper

                    Tracer

                    Siren386
                    Browren486

                    Wiredine

                    Servant

                    Debugger
                    Dominator

                    C-Ray Tube

                    Dragerduel
                    Jurafaduel
Flamers           - Blauzen
                    Silvalt
                    Goldine
LifeDeletr        - LifeDeletr

<a id="s14-2-3"></a>

### 14.2.3. Darkspawn

Darkspawn are the non-intelligent manifestations of the Darkness, that have
come into being due to the weakening of the Algo seal. They are unnatural,
unfriendly, demonic creatures that roam areas saturated with the Darkness'
spirit. They are usually immune to most status effects, yet are highly
susceptible to certain instant-death abilities and light effects. They are
often resistant to a certain element or two, yet are usually weak against
opposing elements. Most darkspawn are encountered in later dungeons.
Right Blades      - Ripper
                    Bladeright
Ghosts            - Haunt
                    Spector
                    Phantom
Riders            - Centaur
                    King Saber
                    Dark Rider
Demons            - Gy-Laguiah  (Boss)
                    Lw-Addmer
                    Cula-Bellr  (1)
                    Cula-Bellr  (2)
Left Blades       - Piercer
                    Hakenleft
Undead            - Zombie
                    Ghoul
Rip Fiends        - DimensWorm
                    OuterBeast
Twin Heads        - StoneHeads
                    CrminHeads  (1)
                    CrminHeads  (2)
                    BlindHeads
Dual Blades       - Twinarms
                    Soldrfiend
Prophallus        - Prophallus

<a id="s14-2-4"></a>

### 14.2.4. Evil Beings

Evil beings are the followers of the Darkness, working to wreak havoc and
destruction in Algo to prepare for the Darkness' return. They are usually
humanoid in appearance (although they may be disproportional), yet possess
inhuman strength or abilities. They are similar to darkspawn in their
resistances and weaknesses, although they act with more purpose and are
generally more difficult to defeat. Most evil beings are encountered in
later dungeons, and represent some of the bosses in the game.
Spearmen          - Speard
                    Zios Guard
Mages             - Tech User
                    TechMaster
                    Dark Witch
Sabers            - ShadowSabr
                    FrostSaber
                    BloodSaber
Warlocks          - Juza        (Boss)
                    Greneris
                    Radhin
Zio               - Zio         (Boss)
Sorcerers         - ChaosSorcr  (1-Boss)
                    ChaosSorcr  (2)
                    Illusionst
                    Imagiomage
Witches           - D-Elm-Lars
                    Xe-A-Thoul  (Boss)
                    Le-Faw-Gan
                    Gi-Le-Farg
Lashiec           - Lashiec     (Boss)
Knights           - DarkMaraud
                    DeathBearr (1)
                    DeathBearr (2)
                    ChaosBrngr

<a id="s14-2-5"></a>

### 14.2.5. Unique

- Unique enemies are very few in number, and are one-of-a-kind encounters
- that are usually bosses. They do not readily fall into any of the above
- categories, and are therefore varied in all ways.
- Unique            - Dark Force  (1-Boss)
- Dark Force  (2-Boss)
- Dark Force  (3-Boss)
- Carnivorous Trees (Boss)
- De-Vars     (Boss)
- Sa-Lews     (Boss)
- Re-Faze     (Boss)
- Blue Rappy
- Rappy
- King Rappy  (Boss)
- Alys        (Boss)
- Profound Darkness (Final Boss)

<a id="s14-3"></a>

## 14.3. Bestiary

This is a comprehensive list of every single enemy in Phantasy Star IV,
including bosses, given in alphabetical order for ease of reference.

The layout of each enemy description is as follows:


```
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯  |          ||           ||          |
 E n e m y   N a m e                  |       HP ||       EXP ||      MST |
_____________________________________ |__________||___________||__________|
¯¯¯|¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯|   __________    Item enemy may drop
   | Enemy Type                    |  / Location \
   |                               | |            ¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
   | Encounter: Type of Battle     |(| Where the enemy is encountered
   |                               | | 
   | Number Encountered:     Range |(| ____________
   |_______________________________| |/ Techniques \
   |Fir|Wtr|Nrg|Frc|Grv|Elc|Rad|Lgt|(|              ¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
   |   |>+<|   | - | + |   |   | x | | The enemy's Techniques
   |¯¯¯¯¯¯¯|¯¯¯¯¯¯¯|¯¯¯¯¯¯¯|¯¯¯¯¯¯¯|(| ________
   | Death |Destroy|Cleanse|  EMP  | |/ Skills \
   |   x   |   /   |   /   |   x   |(|          ¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
   |¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯| | The enemy's Skills
   | Paralysis, Sleep & Seals? Yes |(| 
   |_______________________________| |_____________________________________
   |¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
```

| NOTES: Any additional information about the enemy
   |_______________________________________________________________________

The section between Number Encountered and the Notes gives details of the
enemy's weaknesses and resistances. The first row of eight boxes represents
the eight elements in the game, in the following order:

Fire   Water   Energy   Force   Gravity   Electric   Radiation   Light
 Fir    Wtr     Nrg      Frc     Grv       Elc        Rad         Lgt

Any symbols underneath each element correspond to a certain affinity, as
follows (no symbol indicates the enemy receives normal damage):

x   Immunity   - the enemy takes 1 HP damage from this element

-   Resistance - the enemy takes reduced damage from this element

+   Weakness   - the enemy takes increased damage from this element
 >+<             - extreme weakness - may take as much as double damage

XXX  Unknown    - this element cannot be used at the time

The rows beneath the elements indicate the enemy's susceptibility to the
various death and status effects. A tick (/) means that the enemy can be
affected, and a cross (x) shows that it is immune. A 'Yes' or 'No' in the
bottom box says if the enemy can be affected by Paralysis, Sleep and Seals.

In the above example, the enemy is weak against water and gravity (very
weak against water), resistant to force and immune from light. It can be
affected by destroy and cleanse abilities, but not death or EMP ones, and
can be paralysed or put to sleep.
To find an enemy more quickly, press CTRL+F and type 'BST' followed by the
initial letter of the enemy. For example, to find Dominator type 'BSTD' and
press enter. This will take you to the first entry with that letter.
___________________________________    __________  ___________         BSTA

15. Boss Strategies                                                   CBSST

<a id="s15"></a>

# 15. Boss Strategies

Each boss in the game is given its own strategy in the walkthrough and
side mission sections above. This part of the guide is dedicated to the
special battles in Phantasy Star IV, split into six sections covering each
of the five acts of the main game and the side missions.

<a id="s15-1"></a>

## 15.1. Act I

<a id="s15-1-1"></a>

### 15.1.1. Igglanova 1

Met: Academy Basement           Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 300                          Alys: 7
 EXP: 173                          Chaz: 2-3
 MST: 54                           Hahn: 2-3

To defeat the Igglanova quickly, have Alys use her VORTEX skill and Chaz
and Hahn attack in the first round. The Igglanova will spawn a Xanafalgue
every round until there are two on the screen, at which point it will
attack, so make sure that Chaz attacks the Xanafalgue each round and keep
having Alys use VORTEX. Hahn should be attacking whatever necessary
(usually Igglanova) or using RES if anyone needs healing (which shouldn't
happen). Igglanova should go down in four or five rounds.

<a id="s15-1-2"></a>

### 15.1.2. Igglanova 2

Met: In Zema                    Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 300                          Alys: 9-10     Gryz: 9
 EXP: 173                          Chaz: 9
 MST: 54                           Hahn: 9

The Igglanova is extremely easy this time. The recommended levels given
above are only there because this should be the state of play when you
fight. Don't waste Techniques or Skills. Just have everyone attack the
Igglanova. When it spawns Xanafalgues, Alys will easily destroy them with
her TITNSLASHRs. This battle will be over in a couple of rounds.

<a id="s15-2"></a>

## 15.2. Act II

<a id="s15-2-1"></a>

> 🏅 **Limit: Juza** — Defeat Juza. Combined level limit: 45, party of 5. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_


### 15.2.1. Juza

Met: Zio's Fort                 Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 1523                         Alys: 14-15    Gryz: 15-16
 EXP: 5150                         Chaz: 15-16    Rika: 14-15
 MST: 800                          Hahn: 14-15

In the first round, have Alys use VORTEX, Chaz use CROSSCUT, Hahn use WAT,
Gryz use WAR CRY and Rika use DBLSLASH. This will inflict a fair amount of
damage and increase Gryz's ATK for the rounds to come. In the rounds that
follow, use the same attack strategy. Let Gryz just attack each round, and
Chaz use TSU if he runs out of CROSSCUT.

Juza only uses magic, so have Hahn or Rika heal when a character is hit by
a targeted spell. If Juza uses ZAN, CORROSION or FORCEFLASH (especially the
latter), it may be best to let both of them heal, and maybe even get Chaz
to lend a hand if necessary. Although Gryz has the most HP at this time,
give him priority over other characters as he will take the most damage
from Juza. If you are unlucky and one of your characters falls in this
battle, get a fast character to use the MOON-DEW and a slower one to follow
this up with GIRES or a DIMATE. This should restore them back to a decent
level of health.

If you keep the pressure on Juza, and heal when necessary, this battle
shouldn't last more than four or five rounds.

<a id="s15-2-2"></a>

> 🏅 **The Dark Sorcerer** — Defeat Zio. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_
> 🏅 **Limit: Zio** — Defeat Zio. Combined level limit: 75, party of 5. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_


### 15.2.2. Zio 1

Met: Zio's Fort                 Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: N/A                          N/A
 EXP: N/A
 MST: N/A

You will not win this fight, and you are not meant to. Before you get a
chance to do anything, Zio will use MAG.BARRIR, reducing any magical damage
you inflict to 1 (you won't even hit him with regular attacks).

The simplest way to get through the battle is to let everyone attack each
round (use Macro A if you haven't changed it). In the first round, Zio will
set his hands on fire (no effect), and do nothing in the second round. In
the round that follows he will summon NIGHTMARE, then use BLACK WAVE on
Chaz in the round after that. The battle ends abruptly with a cut-scene.

<a id="s15-2-3"></a>

> 🏅 **Limit: Gy-Laguiah** — Defeat the Gy-Laguiah in Ladea Tower. Combined level limit: 65, party of 5. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_


### 15.2.3. Gy-Laguiah 1

Met: Ladea Tower                Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 2580                         Chaz: 17-18    Demi: 14-15
 EXP: 10000                        Gryz: 17-18    Rune: 20
 MST: 1224                         Rika: 17-18

Not a particularly difficult opponent, as both of its attacks only affect
one character. In the first round, have Chaz use GITHU (if he is not Level
17 yet, which he should be, use CROSSCUT), Gryz use WAR CRY, Rika use SANER
(to ensure that Gy-Laguiah acts last in the round), Demi use her one round
of PHONON, and Rune use GIWAT.

In the subsequent rounds, have Chaz continue to use GITHU or CROSSCUT, let
Gryz just attack, get Rika to heal whoever was attacked in the round before
(unless it was Demi), get Demi to just attack, and keep Rune using GIWAT.
If Demi is attacked, have her use RECOVER in the following round. If any of
your party fall (due to a critical strike), let Demi use MEDIC PW and
follow this up with a curative Technique.

If you keep on top of things, there shouldn't be a problem in this battle,
and it should be over in about five to seven rounds.

<a id="s15-2-4"></a>

### 15.2.4. Zio 2

Met: Nurvus                     Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 2889                         Chaz: 19-20    Demi: 16-17
 EXP: 25999                        Gryz: 19-20    Rune: 21-22
 MST: 1                            Rika: 19-20

Before initiating this battle, set up the following Macro:
Rune: Use Item  - PSYCO-WAND
Gryz: Skill     - WAR CRY
Demi: Skill     - BARRIER
Rika: Technique - DEBAN
Chaz: Skill     - CROSSCUT
As before, Zio will set up his MAG.BARRIR at the very beginning of combat,
nullifying all of your attacks. However, this time you have a trick up your
sleeve. Go to the Macro menu and select the Macro you made above. In the
first round that follows, Zio will summon NIGHTMARE, Rune will cancel the
magical barrier with the PSYCO-WAND, Gryz will enhance his ATK, Demi will
create your own barrier, Rika will further amplify this by increasing the
party's DFS, and Chaz will start the ball rolling with an attack.

From this point Zio will begin his offensive. His arsenal includes Hewn,
Corrosion, Black Wave, and a nameless red energy beam. The first two of
these inflict damage on all the characters (although little on Rune), and
Black Wave and the red beam deal a lot of damage to one character.

In the second round, let Chaz use CROSSCUT again, have Gryz attack, get
Rika to use SANER to make sure everyone gets to act before Zio, have Demi
use her PHONON, and let Rune use GIFOI. In the following rounds, Chaz
should continue using CROSSCUT (or GITHU if he runs out), Gryz should
attack constantly, Rika should use GIRES, Demi should attack, and Rune
should keep on firing GIFOI.

Get Rika to heal characters low on HP, taking into account Zio only uses
magic and that Gryz has very poor magic defence and Rune's magic defence is
very good. Always use Demi's RECOVER Skill if her HP gets low, and in dire
circumstances it may be a good idea to use some DIMATEs and let Chaz do
some healing, or even use Demi's MEDIC PW or a STAR-DEW. Whatever happens,
try to keep your characters conscious. Losing a character means that in the
following round both they and the character that revives them lose a turn.

If you watch your health and keep bearing down on Zio, there's no reason
for the battle to last more than eight to ten rounds.

<a id="s15-2-5"></a>

### 15.2.5. ChaosSorcr

Met: Shuttle                    Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 460                          Chaz: 19-20    Wren: 20
 EXP: 18380                        Rika: 19-20
 MST: 1200                         Rune: 21-22

A break in the pattern of increasing boss difficulty, the ChaosSorcr is
exceptionally easy to defeat. The ChaosSorcr will either use a laser beam
attack, Flaeli, Hewn or ShadowBind (a target-all Skill that has a small
chance of reducing the Agility of each character). Have all the characters
use their standard attacks, and the ChaosSorcr will go down in the second
round, probably only getting the chance to act once in the entire battle.

<a id="s15-3"></a>

## 15.3. Act III

<a id="s15-3-1"></a>

> 🏅 **Limit: Dark Force I** — Defeat Dark Force I. Combined level limit: 113, party of 5. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_
> 🏅 **Limit: Dark Force II** — Defeat Dark Force II. Combined level limit: 140, party of 5. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_
> 🏅 **Limit: Dark Force III** — Defeat Dark Force III. Combined level limit: 115, party of 4. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_


### 15.3.1. Dark Force 1

Met: Kuran                      Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 4540                         Chaz: 25       Wren: 24
 EXP: 32600                        Rika: 26-27    Raja: 27
 MST: 1                            Rune: 25

In the first round, let Chaz use GITHU, Rika use SANER, Rune use NAFOI (or
NAWAT if he is Level 26), Wren use BARRIER and Raja use BLESSING. This
should inflict a decent 400-500 HP of damage on Dark Force, and also
prepare you for the rounds to come.

Dark Force will use either FLARE SHOT (an extremely powerful beam attack
that targets one character), PHONONMASR or BURSTROC (both of which are
fairly damaging hit-all spells).

In the rounds that follow, keep Chaz using GITHU, let Rika use DBLSLASH,
have Rune continue to use NAFOI or NAWAT, continue attacking with Wren,
and get Raja to maintain the party with healing Techniques.

If Dark Force uses FLARE SHOT in the previous round, get Raja to use
GIRES on the victim (or get Wren to use RECOVER if he was hit). If Dark
Force uses one of his party attacks, have Raja use SAR. In the unfortunate
event that a character should fall, have a fast character use REVER or a
MOON-DEW (if you have any) and get a slow character to heal them with GIRES
or a DIMATE. If Wren is the flatlined character, use a REPAIR-KIT.

If you are in a situation where Wren is using RECOVER to heal and everyone
else is at maximum HP, let Raja throw out a ST. FIRE, as this Skill hurts
Dark Force a lot.

Use this strategy, keeping your party's HP levels high and continually
pummelling your opponent, and Dark Force should crumble to dust after a
mere six or seven rounds.

<a id="s15-3-2"></a>

### 15.3.2. Gy-Laguiah 2

Met: Climate Control Centre     Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 2580                         Chaz: 26       Wren: 25
 EXP: 10000                        Rika: 27-28    Raja: 28
 MST: 1224                         Rune: 26

As the Gy-Laguiah is no different from his debut fight, this battle should
be very easy. Don't bother with defensive preparations. Just have Chaz use
GITHU, Rika use DBLSLASH, Rune use NAWAT, Wren use FLARE, and Raja use RES
on the character hit in the round before. Ignore Wren getting damaged, as
the Gy-Laguiah will not be able to kill him before it is defeated.

Without needing to deviate from this pattern, the battle will conclude
after three or four rounds.

<a id="s15-3-3"></a>

### 15.3.3. D-Elm-Lars

Met: Climate Control Centre     Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 777                          Chaz: 27       Wren: 26
 EXP: 3919                         Rika: 28-29    Raja: 29
 MST: 500                          Rune: 26-27

This fellow is ridiculously easy. All you need to do in this battle is
have Chaz, Rika and Wren attack, and let Rune and Raja just defend. Even
doing this, the battle will only last a couple of rounds.

<a id="s15-3-4"></a>

> 🥈 **Limit: Carnivorous Trees** — Defeat 50 Carnivorous Trees without Raja or Kyra. Combined level limit: 95, party of 4. _(RetroAchievements · 10 pts)_


### 15.3.4. Carnivorous Trees

Met: South of Garuberk Tower    Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 240                          N/A
 EXP: N/A
 MST: N/A

There are three Carnivorous Trees. Individually, they are not particularly
dangerous enemies. The only thing they do each round is attack (sometimes
inflicting Poison). However, each time a Carnivorous Tree is defeated it is
replaced with a new one. This cycle never, ever ends, and eventually the
party will be wiped out. Unlike all other boss battles, you can run from
this battle, and this is exactly what you should do. Don't do anything in
the first round except escape. There is no point fighting at all, as you
cannot possibly win. Just run.

<a id="s15-4"></a>

## 15.4. Act IV

<a id="s15-4-1"></a>

> 🏅 **Limit: Xe-A-Thouls** — Defeat the Xe-A-Thouls in Air Castle. Combined level limit: 125, party of 5. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_


### 15.4.1. Xe-A-Thouls

Met: Air Castle                 Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 1520                         Chaz: 36       Wren: 34
 EXP: 7374                         Rika: 38-39    Kyra: 34-35
 MST: 1000                         Rune: 34

Unless you are prepared and use the strategy given below, this will be an
exceptionally tough battle, and definitely the most difficult you will have
faced so far. If you are prepared, however, you may find that the battle is
no harder than the others. Even on their own, a Xe-A-Thoul is considerably
powerful, but together they can combine their power to inflict a severe
amount of damage on the entire party. The most important things to do first
in this battle are to set up a Barrier to reduce your characters' damage
and to drop the Xe-A-Thouls' number to two.

In the first round, have Chaz use RAYBLADE, Rika use DBLSLASH, Rune use
EFESS, Wren use BARRIER, and Kyra use NAFOI. Make sure all three of the
single-target attacks are aimed at the same Xe-A-Thoul. This should inflict
around 1300-1350 HP of damage on that Xe-A-Thoul. Hopefully, Wren will be
able to set up his BARRIER before the Xe-A-Thouls can unleash their
combination attack, THNDRBLAST. Otherwise, each member of your party will
suffer a great deal of damage. Also, one or two of the Xe-A-Thouls may use
GIWAT or GIZAN, or they may just attack.

In the following rounds, have Chaz use AIRSLASH, Rika use SAR (or GISAR if
the party are very hurt), Rune continue to use EFESS, Wren use BURSTROC (or
RECOVER if he is low on HP), and Kyra use HEWN (or an appropriate curative
Technique if necessary). After your party has unleashed their first attack
or two, the most damaged Xe-A-Thoul will fall. This prevents them using
THNDRBLAST again. From now on, the battle will be much easier.

Keep following the above pattern, ensuring each member of your party stays
above half of their maximum HP, and the witches will be finished in a mere
three or four rounds.

<a id="s15-4-2"></a>

> 🏅 **Limit: Lashiec** — Defeat Lashiec. Combined level limit: 133, party of 5. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_


### 15.4.2. Lashiec

Met: Air Castle Basement        Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 6383                         Chaz: 36-37    Wren: 34-35
 EXP: 29999                        Rika: 39-40    Kyra: 34-35
 MST: 1                            Rune: 34-35

In the first round, get Chaz to use RAYBLADE, have Rika use SANER, let
Rune throw out an EFESS, have Wren set up a BARRIER, and get Kyra to use
WARLA. This should set up a decent defence and also start the offensive
against Lashiec.

Lashiec will use one of a few different Skills to begin with - either
THNDHALBRT or ANOTHRGATE (both of which are powerful hit-all Skills, the
latter being the most damaging), or POSSESSION (a single-target Skill that
inflicts Sleep on one character). In the following rounds, have Chaz keep
using RAYBLADE (or NATHU when this runs out), get Rika to use GISAR or
NARES (depending on who was damaged in the round before), get Rune to
continue using EFESS (or NAFOI when this runs out), let Wren just attack
(or use RECOVER if he needs HP), and keep Krya using NAFOI (or GIRES or
a curative item if you need a little extra healing).

Once Lashiec gets to 1/4 HP, he will use REINFORCE, which increases all of
his statistics. This makes him that extra bit tougher, but indicates that
he's almost down. Keep using the above strategy, putting a little more
emphasis on healing if you need it, or letting Rika use DBLSLASH if there
is no healing to be done.

If any of your characters go down, get a fast character to use REVER or a
MOON-DEW, and follow this up with a slower character using GIRES or a
DIMATE or TRIMATE. Alternatively, just use a SOL-DEW or a REPAIR-KIT.

Keep pummelling Lashiec and maintaining your party's HP levels, and this
ancient king will be dethroned in about six or seven rounds.

<a id="s15-4-3"></a>

### 15.4.3. Dark Force 2

Met: Garuberk Tower             Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 7524                         Chaz: 38-39       Wren: 36
 EXP: 46383                        Rika: 40-41       Kyra: 36-37
 MST: 1                            Rune: 35

In the first round, get Chaz to use his RAYBLADE, let Rika use SANER, have
Rune fire his sole LEGEON, get Wren to set up a BARRIER, and have Kyra use
WARLA. This will set up the party for the following rounds, ensuring Dark
Force acts last, and also scratch the surface of Dark Force's HP total.

Dark Force has a different range of abilities this time, including a Skill
that sends a character to Sleep (EVIL EYE), a very damaging beam that hits
one character (SHDWBREATH), and a powerful hit-all attack (LIGHTSHOWR).
Hopefully, Wren will be able to set up his BARRIER before Dark Force uses
SHDWBREATH or LIGHTSHOWR, or you may find that you receive a crippling
amount of damage (including the possibility of immediate flat-lining).

In the following rounds, keep Chaz using RAYBLADE (or NATHU when he runs
out), let Rika use either SAR or GISAR following a LIGHTSHOWR (don't use
NASAR as it will not be necessary at this stage of the game), or GIRES or
NARES following SHDWBREATH, have Rune use EFESS (or NAWAT once the supply
is depleted), get Wren to attack or use RECOVER if needed, and let Kyra use
NAFOI or provide some additional healing. If the organic members of your
party do not need healing, have Rika add to the offence by using DBLSLASH.

If any of the party fall, follow the usual fast character revival and slow
character healing strategy, or use a SOL-DEW if you need to revive quickly.

Try not to let a character's HP stay below half their maximum total, as
there is the possibility that a single attack from Dark Force may knock
them down. Also, if any of the characters succumb to Dark Force's EVIL EYE,
let wake up naturally (don't use Rune's AROWS as this will waste his turn).

Stay offensive and heal quickly, and you'll find that the battle will be
over in around eight to ten rounds.

<a id="s15-5"></a>

## 15.5. Act V

<a id="s15-5-1"></a>

### 15.5.1. Dark Force 3

Met: Near Soldiers' Temple      Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 8240                         Chaz: 41-42       Wren: 38-39
 EXP: 49999                        Rika: 43-44
 MST: 1                            Rune: 38

In the first round, set up the standard defence by getting Chaz to use his
RAYBLADE, having Rika increase the party's Agility by using SANER, letting
Rune let loose an EFESS, and having Wren set up a BARRIER. Hopefully, Wren
will create the BARRIER before Dark Force uses a damaging Skill, else one
or all of the characters will take a severe beating.

Dark Force has exactly the same Skills that Seth had (except DTHSPELL),
including CORRSION (this hit-all Skill is far more powerful this time),
SHADOWBIND (reducing the Agility of all organic characters) and MINDBLST
(a hit-all Skill that may inflict Sleep on each character). It also has a
normal, fairly damaging, attack.

In the second round, get Chaz to use RAYBLADE again, have Rika use DEBAN,
get Rune to unleash another EFESS, and have Wren just attack normally. If
the party need healing in this round, get Wren to use a STAR-DEW instead of
attacking. If only one character is injured, let him use a TRIMATE or his
RECOVER Skill.

In the following rounds, keep Chaz using RAYBLADE (or NATHU when this runs
out), let Rika take over the healing by using SAR, GISAR or GIRES (or NASAR
or NARES if necessary), have Rune use EFESS (or LEGEON or NAWAT when you
run out), and get Wren to attack or use RECOVER on himself.

As usual, let Rika throw out a DBLSLASH if no healing needs to be done, and
do not use AROWS if any characters fall asleep. After all, it is likely
that any characters that don't wake up immediately will wake up in the next
round. Using AROWS would just be a waste of a chance to use one of Rune's
powerful offensive spells.

If Rika falls asleep and there is healing to be done, get Wren to cover for
her by using a STAR-DEW or a TRIMATE, or let Chaz use one of his curative
Techniques if you are low on items.

Try to keep every characters' HP above half their maximum value at all
times, and if one of your party members is flatlined, follow the standard
fast/slow revival strategy or use a SOL-DEW or a REPAIR-KIT.

A little more care may need to be taken in this battle, as Dark Force's
Sleep-inflicting Skill may take characters out of commission for a round or
two on a fairly regular basis. It may be necessary to postpone attacking
Dark Force for an entire round if healing needs to be done.

This battle will very likely take a lot longer than any of the previous
boss battles, and possibly use a few items in the process, but if you keep
the characters at a safe HP level, it should all be over in around ten to
thirteen rounds.

<a id="s15-5-2"></a>

> 🥈 **Limit: De-Vars** — Defeat De-Vars. Combined level limit: 125, party of 4. _(RetroAchievements · 10 pts)_


### 15.5.2. De-Vars

Met: Strength Tower             Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 5499                         Chaz: 43-46       Wren: 40-43
 EXP: 35000                        Rika: 46-49
 MST: 1                            Rune: 40-42

The guardian of the Strength Tower, De-Vars is a master of physical combat.
In the first round, have Chaz use RAYBLADE, get Rika to set up DEBAN, let
Rune use LEGEON, and get Wren to just attack normally (a BARRIER would be a
waste of time, as De-Vars doesn't use magical attacks). De-Vars will either
perform a standard attack or unleash a hit-all Skill called DISRUPTARM.

In the following rounds, let Chaz continue using his RAYBLADE (or NATHU if
this is exhausted), get Rika to use GIRES or GISAR (you won't need more
powerful healing than this), get Rune to use LEGEON (or NAWAT if this runs
out), and keep Wren attacking (or use RECOVER if he is low on HP).

As usual, have Rika perform DBLSLASH if there is no organic healing to be
done, and revive fallen characters with the fast-slow method, a SOL-DEW or
a REPAIR-KIT (for Wren).

Follow the strategy above, and De-Vars will concede in around seven or
eight rounds.

<a id="s15-5-3"></a>

> 🥈 **Limit: Sa-Lews** — Defeat Sa-Lews. Combined level limit: 125, party of 4. _(RetroAchievements · 10 pts)_


### 15.5.3. Sa-Lews

Met: Courage Tower              Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 5499                         Chaz: 43-46       Wren: 40-43
 EXP: 35000                        Rika: 46-49
 MST: 1                            Rune: 40-42

The guardian of the Courage Tower, Sa-Lews is a master of magical combat.
In the first round, have Chaz use CROSSCUT, get Rika to use SANER, let Rune
use LEGEON, and get Wren to set up his BARRIER.

Sa-Lews will use a number of Rune's Skills, including FLAELI, HEWN, TANDLE
and LEGEON. As three of these are hit-all Skills, you may be in for a tough
time in this battle.

In the following rounds, let Chaz continue using his CROSSCUT, get Rika to
use GIRES or GISAR (you may need to use NASAR following some of Sa-Lews
attacks), get Rune to use LEGEON (or NAWAT if this runs out), and keep Wren
attacking (or use RECOVER if he is low on HP).

As usual, have Rika perform DBLSLASH if there is no organic healing to be
done, and revive fallen characters with the fast-slow method, a SOL-DEW or
a REPAIR-KIT (for Wren).

Follow the strategy above, and Sa-Lews will concede in around seven or
eight rounds.

<a id="s15-5-4"></a>

> 🏅 **The End of the Millennium** — Defeat the Profound Darkness. _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_
> 🥈 **Profound Courage** — Take Hahn and defeat the Profound Darkness. _(RetroAchievements · 10 pts)_
> 🥈 **Profound Strength** — Take Gryz and defeat the Profound Darkness. _(RetroAchievements · 10 pts)_
> 🥈 **Profound Will** — Take Demi and defeat the Profound Darkness. _(RetroAchievements · 10 pts)_
> 🥈 **Profound Wit** — Take Raja and defeat the Profound Darkness. _(RetroAchievements · 10 pts)_
> 🥈 **Profound Spirit** — Take Kyra and defeat the Profound Darkness. _(RetroAchievements · 10 pts)_
> 🏅 **Four Bells, Four Torches** — Defeat the Profound Darkness with only the main 4 characters. (Missed if anyone else is taken.) _(RetroAchievements · 25 pts)_
> 🏅 **Limit: Profound Darkness** — Defeat the Profound Darkness. Combined level limit: 170 with a party of 5, or 155 with a party of 4. _(RetroAchievements · 50 pts)_


### 15.5.4. Profound Darkness

Met: The Edge                   Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 4120/4620/12999              Chaz: 49+         Wren: 46+
 EXP: N/A                          Rika: 52+        Other: 45+
 MST: N/A                          Rune: 45+

The final boss battle of the game consists of three stages, each involving
combat with one of the incarnations of The Profound Darkness. They all
differ in their strength and abilities, so this strategy guide will explain
each incarnation separately. Also, the fifth character you have chosen will
determine the best method of fighting The Profound Darkness, so there are
five different strategies representing each possible choice. Good luck!

Stage 1 - The first incarnation is fairly unsettling it its appearance, but
          it is the weakest of the three. It will use only single-target
          attacks, including RAY-BREATH, FIREBREATH and SHDWBREATH. They
          are fairly similar in their strength, but certain characters will
          be weaker or more resistant to certain attacks. You will only
          need to use single-target healing to overcome these Skills.

Hahn - In the first round, have Chaz use RAYBLADE, Rika use SANER to
          speed up the party, Rune use NAWAT, Wren throw up a BARRIER, and
          Hahn use his VISION Skill.

In the second round, get Chaz to use RAYBLADE again, let Rika use
          DEBAN, have Rune use NAWAT, have Wren just attack or use RECOVER,
          and let Hahn use GIRES or NARES (or NAWAT if Wren uses RECOVER).

In the following rounds, keep Chaz using RAYBLADE, have Rika take
          over the healing (or use DBLSLASH if no healing is required), let
          Rune continue using NAWAT, get Wren to attack or use RECOVER, and
          have Hahn use NAWAT as well.

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          second form appears, which should take no more than six rounds.

Gryz - In the first round, have Chaz use RAYBLADE, Rika use SANER to
          speed up the party, Rune use NAWAT, Wren throw up a BARRIER, and
          Gryz perform a WAR CRY.

In the second round, get Chaz to use GIRES or NARES (or RAYBLADE
          if Wren uses RECOVER), let Rika use DEBAN, have Rune use NAWAT,
          have Wren just attack or use RECOVER, and let Gryz just attack.

In the following rounds, get Chaz to use RAYBLADE, have Rika take
          over the healing (or use DBLSLASH if no healing is required), let
          Rune continue using NAWAT, get Wren to attack or use RECOVER, and
          have Gryz attack as well.

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          second form appears, which should take no more than six rounds.

Demi - In the first round, have Chaz use RAYBLADE, Rika use SANER to
          speed up the party, Rune use NAWAT, Wren attack normally, and
          Demi set up a BARRIER.

In the second round, get Chaz to use GIRES or NARES (or RAYBLADE
          if Wren uses RECOVER), let Rika use DEBAN, have Rune use NAWAT,
          have Wren just attack or use RECOVER, and let Demi just attack or
          use RECOVER too.

In the following rounds, get Chaz to use RAYBLADE, have Rika take
          over the healing (or use DBLSLASH if no healing is required), let
          Rune continue using NAWAT, get Wren to attack or use RECOVER, and
          have Demi attack or use RECOVER as well.

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          second form appears, which should take no more than six rounds.

Raja - In the first round, have Chaz use RAYBLADE, Rika use SANER to
          speed up the party, Rune use NAWAT, Wren throw up a BARRIER, and
          Raja use BLESSING.

In the second round, get Chaz to use RAYBLADE, let Rika perform a
          DBLSLASH, have Rune use NAWAT, have Wren attack or use RECOVER,
          and let Raja use RES or GIRES (or defend if Wren uses RECOVER).

In the following rounds, get Chaz to use RAYBLADE, have Rika keep
          using DBLSLASH, let Rune continue using NAWAT, get Wren to attack
          or use RECOVER, and have Raja continue the healing.

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          second form appears, which should take no more than six rounds.

Kyra - In the first round, have Chaz use RAYBLADE, Rika use SANER to
          speed up the party, Rune use NAWAT, Wren throw up a BARRIER, and
          Kyra use her WARLA Skill.

In the second round, get Chaz to use RAYBLADE, let Rika use GIRES
          or NARES (or DBLSLASH if no healing is required), have Rune use
          NAWAT, have Wren attack or use RECOVER, and let Kyra use NAFOI.

In the following rounds, get Chaz to use RAYBLADE, have Rika keep
          up the healing or using DBLSLASH, let Rune continue using NAWAT,
          get Wren to attack or use RECOVER, and have Kyra use NAFOI.

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          second form appears, which should take no more than six rounds.

Stage 2 - The second incarnation has only slightly more HP than the first,
          but has far more powerful Skills. Apart from a lightning-style
          normal attack, the second form has use of DISTORTION, LIGHTSHOWR
          and ANOTHRGATE. These three Skills deal a considerable amount of
          damage to all members of the party, so target-all healing will be
          the order of the day this time. As there is no initial setup to
          be done, the second stage shouldn't last as long as the first.

Hahn - From the beginning, keep Chaz using RAYBLADE (or CROSSCUT when
          this runs out), have Rika use GIRES or GISAR (or use DBLSLASH if
          no healing is required), let Rune continue using NAWAT, get Wren
          to attack or use RECOVER, and have Hahn use NAWAT as well.

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          final form appears, which should take no more than five rounds.

Gryz - From the beginning, keep Chaz using RAYBLADE (or CROSSCUT when
          this runs out), have Rika use GIRES or GISAR (or use DBLSLASH if
          no healing is required), let Rune continue using NAWAT, get Wren
          to attack or use RECOVER, and have Gryz just attack as well.

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          final form appears, which should take no more than five rounds.

Demi - From the beginning, keep Chaz using RAYBLADE (or CROSSCUT when
          this runs out), have Rika use GIRES or GISAR (or use DBLSLASH if
          no healing is required), let Rune continue using NAWAT, have Wren
          attack or use RECOVER, and get Demi to use PHONOMEZER or RECOVER.

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          final form appears, which should take no more than five rounds.

Raja - From the beginning, keep Chaz using RAYBLADE (or CROSSCUT when
          this runs out), have Rika use DBLSLASH, let Rune continue using
          NAWAT, get Wren to attack or use RECOVER, and have Raja keep up
          his expert healing by using a RES or a SAR (or else just defend).

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          final form appears, which should take no more than five rounds.

Kyra - From the beginning, keep Chaz using RAYBLADE (or CROSSCUT when
          this runs out), have Rika use GIRES or GISAR (or use DBLSLASH if
          no healing is required), let Rune continue using NAWAT, get Wren
          to attack or use RECOVER, and have Kyra keep using NAFOI.

Keep using this strategy until the incarnation dissipates and the
          final form appears, which should take no more than five rounds.

Stage 3 - The third and final incarnation of The Profound Darkness is the
          toughest of them all, and with about three times as many HP it
          will definitely take the longest. It has a standard attack which
          is fairly damaging, and a few other abilities as well. These
          consist of POSSESSION (that may inflict Sleep on a character),
          CANCELING (extremely annoying, as it removes all assistance
          effects from the party such as BARRIER, DEBAN, SANER, etc.), and
          the powerful MEGID Technique. Don't hold back. This is it.

Hahn - From the beginning, have Chaz use MEGID (or CROSSCUT if you can't
          use this Technique), get Rika to take care of the healing (or use
          DBLSLASH if healing isn't required), let Rune throw out a LEGEON
          (or EFESS when this runs out), get Wren to use POSIBOLT if he has
          it (else attack, using RECOVER when needed), and have Hahn use
          his ASTRAL Skill (or NAWAT when the stock is depleted).

After CANCELING, have Rika use DEBAN instead of healing, let Wren
          use BARRIER instead of attacking or healing, and get Hahn to
          cover the curative responsibility by using NARES or an item.

If Rika runs out of TP from healing, have Hahn take over by using
          Techs, or by dipping into your (hopefully extensive) item supply.

Keep using this strategy until The Profound Darkness is finally
          destroyed, which should between nine to twelve rounds.

Gryz - From the beginning, have Chaz use MEGID (or CROSSCUT if you can't
          use this Technique), get Rika take care of the healing (or use
          DBLSLASH if healing isn't required), let Rune throw out a LEGEON
          (or EFESS when this runs out), get Wren to use POSIBOLT if he has
          it (else attack, using RECOVER when needed), and have Grzy keep
          attacking (this is his forte).

After CANCELING, have Rika use DEBAN instead of healing, let Wren
          use BARRIER instead of attacking or healing, and get Gryz to
          cover the curative responsibility by using appropriate items.

If Rika runs out of TP from healing, have Gryz take over the job
          by dipping into your (hopefully extensive) item supply.

Keep using this strategy until The Profound Darkness is finally
          destroyed, which should between nine to twelve rounds.

Demi - From the beginning, have Chaz use MEGID (or CROSSCUT if you can't
          use this Technique), get Rika take care of the healing (or use
          DBLSLASH if healing isn't required), let Rune throw out a LEGEON
          (or EFESS when this runs out), get Wren to use POSIBOLT if he has
          it (else attack, using RECOVER when needed), and have Demi use
          PHONOMEZER if she can (else attack, using RECOVER when needed).

After CANCELING, have Rika use DEBAN instead of healing, let Wren
          use BARRIER instead of attacking or healing, and get Demi to
          cover the curative responsibility by using MEDIC PW or an item.

If Rika runs out of TP from healing, have Demi take over with her
          MEDIC PW or by utilizing your (hopefully extensive) item supply.

Keep using this strategy until The Profound Darkness is finally
          destroyed, which should between nine to twelve rounds.

Raja - From the beginning, have Chaz use MEGID (or CROSSCUT if you can't
          use this Technique), get Rika to keep using DBLSLASH (or attack
          when the stock is exhausted), let Rune throw out a LEGEON (or
          EFESS when this runs out), get Wren to use POSIBOLT if he has
          it (else attack, using RECOVER when needed), and have Raja keep
          using curative Techs (or ST. FIRE if no healing is required).

After CANCELING, have Rika use DEBAN instead of attacking, and
          let Wren use BARRIER instead of attacking or healing.

If Raja runs out of TP from healing, have Rika take over for a
          round while Raja uses ATARAXIA on himself to regain some TP.

Keep using this strategy until The Profound Darkness is finally
          destroyed, which should between nine to twelve rounds.

Kyra - From the beginning, have Chaz use MEGID (or CROSSCUT if you can't
          use this Technique), get Rika take care of the healing (or use
          DBLSLASH if healing isn't required), let Rune throw out a LEGEON
          (or EFESS when this runs out), get Wren to use POSIBOLT if he has
          it (else attack, using RECOVER when needed), and have Kyra use
          TANDLE (or NAFOI if this runs out).

After CANCELING, have Kyra use WARLA instead of attacking, and
          let Wren use BARRIER instead of attacking or healing.

If Rika runs out of TP from healing, have Kyra take over with her
          Techs or by dipping into your (hopefully extensive) item supply.

Keep using this strategy until The Profound Darkness is finally
          destroyed, which should between nine to twelve rounds.

<a id="s15-6"></a>

## 15.6. Side Missions

<a id="s15-6-1"></a>

> 🥈 **Limit: Fissure Fract Ooze** — Defeat the Fract Ooze in 'Fissure of Fear' before finding Wren. Combined level limit: 55, party of 3. _(RetroAchievements · 10 pts)_


### 15.6.1. Fract Ooze

Met: The Hole                   Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 1999                         Party: 19
 EXP: 42236
 MST: 855

Use your best Skills and Techniques to get the battle over as quickly as
possible, avoiding light Skills as the Fract Ooze is resistant to these.

Apart from its standard attack, the Fract Ooze only uses one Skill called
CELL SPLIT, a hit-all attack that does a small amount of damage. If you
stay on the offensive, it is unlikely you will need to heal at all, and the
battle should be over in no more than two or three rounds.
 Met: Rappy Cave                 Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 2911                         Party: 36
 EXP: 39852
 MST: 555

In the first round, have Chaz use RAYBLADE, let Rika use DEBAN, have Rune
use LEGEON, and get Wren to use BARRIER. If there is another character in
your party, let them perform their best attack (avoiding light Skills).

King Rappy will either use a normal attack or its EARTHQUAKE Skill (which
damages all characters). With the defences set up, neither of these attacks
should pose too much of a threat.

In the rounds that follow, let Chaz continue using RAYBLADE, have Rika use
DBLSLASH, get Rune to use NAWAT, let Wren just attack, and have your other
character (if there is one) use their best abilities.

Obviously, have Wren use RECOVER if he needs to (unlikely), and get Rika to
heal any other characters that drop to low HP levels (also unlikely).

If you keep the pressure on, King Rappy should fly the nest in about four
or five rounds.

<a id="s15-6-3"></a>

### 15.6.3. Dominators

Met: Vahal Fort                 Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: 999                          Party: 37
 EXP: 14400
 MST: 1500

Three Dominators are the sum total of Daughter's defences, and it shouldn't

be a great chore to defeat them. Use hit-all Techniques and Skills (try out
Wren's POSIBOLT), and the Dominators should only last a couple of rounds.

<a id="s15-6-4"></a>

### 15.6.4. Alys

Met: Anger Tower                Recommended Level before fighting:
  HP: Varies                       Chaz: 45-46
 EXP: 1
 MST: 1

Just have Chaz use normal attacks, as Alys should not be able to inflict
enough damage to kill him before she falls.
16. Geography                                                         CGGRP

<a id="s16"></a>

# 16. Geography

<a id="s16-1"></a>

## 16.1. Algo

The entire Phantasy Star IV game is set in the star system of Algo. It is a
fairly small system comprising the star Algo, an asteroid belt formed from
the destruction of the planet Parma, the planets Motavia, Dezolis and
Rykros, and artificial satellites (there are two that are mentioned in the
game, although there could very well be more).

The Algo star itself is fixed on a specific location, and the asteroid
belt, planets and satellites orbit this star. The asteroid belt is the
closest to Algo, as it consists of the debris that resulted from the
destruction of the first planet, Parma, a thousand years ago. A little
further out from the asteroid belt is Motavia, which shares its orbit with
the artificial satellite Zelan. At the outskirts of the Algo system are
Dezolis and the artificial satellite Kuran, which occupy the same orbit as
well. Finally, the planet Rykros orbits the star in a highly elliptical
orbit, passing inside the other planets once every thousand years.

The star system has a unique purpose that it has had since its creation
many thousands of years ago. After the defeat of The Profound Darkness, The
Great Light banished it to a different dimension, and created the Algo
system to seal the portal between the dimensions. This is the secret of
Algo, and the reason for its existence.

<a id="s16-2"></a>

> 🥉 **Elemental Weaknesses** — Execute Combo: Blizzard on Motavia, or Fire Storm on Dezolis. _(RetroAchievements · 3 pts)_


## 16.2. Motavia

Motavia is the second planet of the Algo system, and also the largest. It
is composed of roughly equal areas of land and water, the majority of the
land being sand-covered. It is a naturally hot planet, but suffers greatly
after the environmental control systems go awry. With poor soil and
inhospitable climate conditions, the Motavia seen at the beginning of the
game is not an easy place in which to live.

The indiginous sentient beings on Motavia are the aptly-named Motavians.
These blue, fur-covered humans seem poorly designed for life in a hot
climate, but it seems that their fur must act to reflect heat rather than
insulate. Since the arrival of the Parmanians a thousand years ago, the
Motavian population has dwindled, and now there is only one small village
remaining. They are a strong, proud race, and understandably fearful of
their less furry neighbours. They are also noted for their knowledge of
refining titanium.

Motavia is home to a number of towns and villages, mostly Parmanian, and
also houses a fair few secrets. The game begins on Motavia, and is the main
area of the game for a long while.

<a id="s16-3"></a>

## 16.3. Dezolis

Dezolis is the third planet of the Algo system, but its size is difficult
to determine. Although the party are able to traverse some of its surface,
they are trapped on all sides by mountains. This prevents seeing how big
Dezolis really is. This aside, Dezolis is the climatic opposite of Motavia,
being a very cold planet. Like Motavia, Dezolis has had serious problems
with the climate systems, and this causes the terrible snowstorm seen when
the party first arrives.

The native humanoids on Dezolis are the Dezolisians. They are green,
reptilian humans whose thick skins protect them from the natural cold of
their planet. Like the Motavians, the Dezolisians were also hosts for the
fleeing Parmanians. Luckily for them, however, the Parmanians found life a
little more difficult than their Motavia-bound cousins, so the Dezolisian
population has not seen any problems. They are a fun-loving, intelligent
race, who are well-known for their forging of the rare metal laconia.

Dezolis is home to a number of villages and one town, fairly equally split
between Parmanians and Dezolisians, and also houses a fair few secrets. The
game moves onto Dezolis shortly after acquiring the shuttle, and is the
main area of the game until the snowstorm has been abated.

<a id="s16-4"></a>

## 16.4. Rykros

Rykros is the fourth planet of the Algo system, and easily the smallest. It
is generally unknown to the inhabitants of Algo, as it is kept invisible
and undetectable for most of the time. In addition, the orbit of Rykros is
highly elliptical, passing close to Algo only once every thousand years.
When Rykros returns, it marks the weakening of the seal that is keeping The
Profound Darkness confined in its dimension, but can only be found by using
the light of the Aero-Prism. The Profound Darkness realises the danger that
this planet poses to him, and uses Dark Force (in the guise of Seth) to
discover its location. The Darkness then sends some of his strongest forces
to Rykros in order to stop the party from acquiring the only items that can
withstand his power.

Rykros is home to only a few structures, each of which is forged from the
natural crystal that covers the planet's surface. It is not populated by
any humans, as its only inhabitants are ancient, powerful guardians whose
sole purpose is to protect the Rings of the Stars and pass the knowledge of
the past onto the chosen Protectors. Each of the beings on Rykros command
one of the four structures of the planet. Le Roof is best described as the
lord of Rykros, and his spiritual presence exists inside the Silence
Temple. The other three are powerful entities that can provide the party
with valuable gifts once they are satisfied that the party is worthy to
receive them.

<a id="s16-5"></a>

> 🥉 **A Memento of our Trip** — Place a particular triangular flag in your house and admire it. _(RetroAchievements · 3 pts)_
> 🥉 **The Romance of Travel** — Place a particular wood doll in your house and admire it. _(RetroAchievements · 4 pts)_


## 16.5. Towns and Villages

This section gives a brief description of each town a village in the game,
listed in alphabetical order. It will also include the stores and other
amenities that the settlements have to offer, and other important details.
Aiedo   - Planet:    Motavia
          Location:  Southwest of Nalya and north of Kadary
          Key Areas: Inn, 2 Tool Stores, 4 Weapon Stores, 4 Armour Stores,
                     Hunters' Guild, Naura Cake Shop, Alys' House,
                     Tinkerbell's House, Prison
          Treasure:  1000 MST, TRIMATE

The largest town in the game, Aiedo contains a whole host of
          stores, special locations and interesting people. It is best
          known as the site of the famous Hunters' Guild, and also houses
          a prison, a bar, a cemetery, Alys' house and the Naura Cake Shop.
          There is a fortune-teller that lives in the eastmost house, and
          shop music plays while you are inside. However, there is nothing
          you can buy and you won't get your fortune told, so it seems a
          little strange.

The Market: This massive building in the centre of town houses a
            number of stores and the inn.

Inn: 50 MST per character

Alys' House: Situated in the northwest corner of Aiedo, this
            building is the party's home base. When entered, either Alys or
            Chaz will ask if the party should rest. Selecting 'Yes' fully
            restores the party for free. Alys' House is also the only place
            where the PENNANT and the WOODCARVIN can be used.

Tinkerbell's House: This ordinary house is sited near the river
            in the southeast corner of the town, just to the left of the
            fortune-teller's house. It is the residence of Tinkerbell and
            her parents, involved in the second Hunters' Guild job.

Prison: Directly north of the market, this detention centre is
            the focus of the fifth Hunters' Guild job, as the two daughters
            of the chief of Uzo are locked up here.
Jut     - Planet:    Dezolis
          Location:  Southwest of Gumbious Temple
          Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Weapon Store, Armour Store

Jut is the only town on Dezolis, and is the main Dezolisian
          settlement. It is the site for a few shops and a large central
          church. This church is a little redundant with the Gumbious
          Temple so close by, and has no real purpose in the game.

The Inn can be found in the southeast corner of Jut.

Inn: 150 MST per character

The Tool Store is in the lower west section of Jut, and the
          Weapon and Armour Stores are located in the northeast of town.

- Kadary  - Planet:    Motavia
- Location:  North of Mile and south of Aiedo
- Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Zio's Church

This small village is the site of Zio's cult following at the
          beginning of the game, due to its close proximity to Zio's Fort.
          After Zio's demise, the inhabitants that had fallen under the
          Black Magician's spell are left dazed and lost, and one of these
          unfortunate victims forms the basis for a Hunters' Guild job.
          There is a LASRSLASHR in the northeast building in Kadary, that
          can only be accessed by walking around the village wall.

The Inn can be found in the southeast part of Kadary. In addition
          to its normal function, the party take the student girl back to
          this Inn after she collapses in the third Hunters' Guild job.

Inn: 40 MST per character

The Tool Store is located in the southwest of the village.

Zio's Church: Dominating the northwest corner of Kadary, this
            large church is the site of Zio's worship until he is defeated.
            It has no real purpose except in the third Hunters' Guild job,
            when the missing student from Piata can be found here.
Krup    - Planet:    Motavia
          Location:  East of Molcum and south of Tonoe
          Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Armour Store

A small and rather quaint village, Krup is Hahn's hometown and
          the place of residence of Hahn's father, mother and fiancee. It
          has a couple of small shops and allows some story developments,
          but it has no essential purpose beyond this. Hahn's parents live
          in the building containing the Armour Store, and Hahn's fiancee
          Saya teaches children at her home on the north side of Krup.
          Krup is also one of the possible sites for Rocky to be found in
          the second Hunters' Guild job.

The Inn can be found in the southeast part of Krup. In addition
          to its normal function, the party take Alys back to this Inn
          after she is hit by Zio's Black Wave.

Inn: 15 MST per character

The Tool Store is on the east side of Krup, and the Armour Store
          is located in the west part of the village.

Meese is a fairly small Parmanian village, which is affected most

          When the party first enter this village, the only area of any
          importance (apart from the usual amenities) is the clinic. There
          is also a Perfume Store that is locked due to the epidemic, and
          won't become accessible until the Garuberk Tower is no more. The
          party will first meet the Espers here, and will also lose Raja
          as he falls ill from the Black Energy Wave.

The Inn is located in the southwest corner of Meese.

The Clinic: Found in the southeast part of the village, this
            former Inn is now a small hospital for the sick residents of
            Meese. The party can interact with any of the people in the
            building, but they must speak to the off-duty Esper in the
            right-hand upstairs room to move the story along. It is here
            that Raja will fall ill and leave the party, and subsequently
            where they will learn of Kyra's attempt to get through the
            carnivorous trees surrounding the Garuberk Tower.

Perfume Store: Until the Garuberk Tower is destroyed, the Perfume
            Store is closed due to the Black Energy Wave. After this, the
            party can sample the unique delights of this store's wares.

Sand Worm Ranch: This area has no special attraction when the

            Worm (easier than its wild cousins) to complete the mission.
Molcum  - Planet:    Motavia
          Location:  South of Zema and west of Krup
          Key Areas: -

This village is dead, once home to a group of Motavians but now
          burnt to the ground by Zio. The party originally go to Molcum to
          obtain the ALSHLINE, but find that there is none there. By way of
          compensation, however, this is the first encounter with Rune, and
          he joins the party in this village.
Monsen  - Planet:    Motavia
          Location:  South of Kadary and northeast of Piata
          Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Crack, Eddie's House

The village of Monsen is plagued by earthquakes when the party
          first visit. This is caused by a malfunction in the Plate System
          to the northeast. Due to the recent tremors, there is a large
          crack in the ground in the southeast corner of the village, but
          the only other point of interest is that Monsen is one of the
          possible sites for Rocky to be found in the second Guild job.

The Inn can be found in the west part of Monsen.

Inn: 45 MST per character

The Tool Store is located in the south area of the village.

Nalya   - Planet:    Motavia
          Location:  Northeast of Aiedo and southwest of Wreckage
          Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store

This village is one of the few in the game that has no direct
          connection with any part of the story. After a metallic object
          crashed into the ground nearby a few months ago, half of the
          settlement was destroyed. The few people who remain in Nalya
          try to continue a fairly normal life, but they are constantly
          wary of their uninvited neighbour.

The Inn can be found in the southeast corner of Nalya.

The game begins in this town, on the second floor of Motavia
          Academy. Piata is informally known as the Town of Learning, and
          is a popular location for scholars. After a research team, sent
          by the academy, returned from an expedition to Birth Valley, the
          town became surrounded by monsters. This situation is the cause
          of Chaz's and Alys' presence in Piata at the beginning.

Motavia Academy: The large building on the north side of Piata is
            the renowned Motavia Academy, and is the centre of knowledge
            for all Motavia. The party begin in the academy, their first
            port of call being the principal's office at the back of the
            second floor. The stairs on the ground floor lead to the first
            dungeon of the game, and this is where Hahn joins the party.

Dormitory: In the third Hunters' Guild mission, the party must

            student. It can be found in the northwest corner of town.
Reshel  - Planet:    Dezolis
          Location:  East of Zosa and northwest of Meese
          Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Armour Store

During the snowstorm on Dezolis, Reshel is a dead town inhabited
          only by Zombies. Once the snowstorm has been abated, however,
          those people that escaped to Meese return to rebuild their small
          village. To begin with, only the Armour Store is open. After the
          party have defeated the third Dark Force, Reshel is once again
          fully restored to its normal state. Apart from this, there is
          nothing particularly special about this village.

The Inn, after the third Dark Force is defeated, is found in the
          south part of Reshel.

Inn: 130 MST per character

The Tool store is open after the Aero-Prism is acquired, and is
          found in the northeast corner of the village. The Armour Store is
          one of the first buildings rebuilt after the Garuberk Tower is
          destroyed, and is located in the southwest.

- Location:  Island south of Termi
- Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Culvers' House, Sekreas' House

This optional village is located on an island south of Termi. It
          is a simple agricultural community that has been afflicted by a
          serious threat in recent times. A flock of vicious birds has
          started eating up all the fields, and the villagers are worried.
          Two of the Hunters' Guild jobs are centred around Torinco, but it
          has no other special purpose beyond these.

The Inn is located in the southwest corner of Torinco.

Inn: 90 MST per character

The Tool store is to be found in the south part of the village.

Tool Store


```
            ----------------
```

- TRIMATE      400
- ANTIDOTE      10
- CURE-PARAL   120
- TELEPIPE     130
- ESCAPIPE      70

Culvers' House: The sixth Hunters' Guild job takes the party to
            the house of Mr. Culvers, located in the northwest corner of
            Torinco. His son has fallen ill, and the party must bring him
            something from Termi in an attempt to make him better.

Sekreas' House: The man behind the bird outbreak is Mr. Sekreas,
            who lives on the east side of the village. Although he sends a
            request to the Guild for the birds to be exterminated, it turns
            out that his real intention is a little different. The party
            must speak to Mr. Sekreas in the seventh Hunters' Guild job.
Tyler   - Planet:    Dezolis
          Location:  Northwest of Ryuon and southwest of Zosa
          Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Weapon Store, Armour Store, Grave

This small village was the first settlement of the Parmanians
          after they crashed on Dezolis. Out of respect for their captian,
          Tyler, they named the village for him and built a huge monument
          in his honour. The party are led to this village on the trail of
          a spaceship to take them to Kuran.

The Inn is located in the southeast corner of Tyler.

Inn: 110 MST per character

The Tool Store is located in the centre of the village, and the
          Weapon and Armour Stores can be found in the northeast.

Tool Store            Weapon Store          Armour Store

Grave: Unless the party speak to Gyuna about the spaceship, the
            grave located in the west section of the village will have no

            the entrance to the Hanger.
Uzo     - Planet:    Motavia
          Location:  Island southwest of Piata
          Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Chief's House

This village is located on a small island to the southwest of
          Piata. Its only link to the story is that it is the source of the
          fifth Hunters' Guild job.

The Inn is located in the northeast corner of Uzo.

Inn: 80 MST per character

The Tool store can be found in the southeast part of the village.

Chief's House: The fifth Hunters' Guild job leads them to the
            house of the chief of Uzo, whose daughters have gone missing.
            They must speak to the chief to get clues about his daughters'
            whereabouts.
Zema    - Planet:    Motavia
          Location:  Northeast of Mile and south of Nalya
          Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Weapon Store, Armour Store,
                     Old Man's House

This village begins as a gallery of stone statues, having been
          recently visited by Zio. Zema is the gateway to Birth Valley,
          where a research team from Piata had gone missing. The party
          must go to Zema to find Professor Holt, but his rocky nature
          takes them on a short quest to obtain Alshline. Once they find
          this medicine, they can return Zema to its normal state. As if
          Zema didn't have enough problems, it also becomes overrun by
          machines later in the game, and this gives rise to the eighth
          Hunters' Guild job.

The Inn is located in the eastern part of Zema.

Inn: 20 MST per character

The Tool Store is situated in the southeast corner of Zema, and
          the Weapon and Armour Stores can be found in the west part.

Old Man's House: After the village is populated with mechanical
            monsters, an old man sends a request to the Guild. In the
            eighth Hunters' Guild job, the party must visit the old man,
            who lives in a house in the northeast corner of Zema, to learn
            more about the situation.
Zosa    - Planet:    Dezolis
          Location:  Northeast of Tyler and west of Reshel
          Key Areas: Inn, Tool Store, Weapon Store, Armour Store,
                     Penguin Man

This unusual Dezolisian village has no special function in the
          game, but it is a useful place to pick up some new equipment
          after the first encounter with Dark Force. It is also home to the
          strange Dezolis Penguin, and is the only place from which
          PENGU-FEED may be purchased.

The Inn is located in the southwest corner of Meese.

Inn: 120 MST per character

The Tool Store is on the west side of Meese, and the Weapon and
          Armour Stores are inside the building in the northwest corner.
          Also note that teleportation is impossible within the Tool Store.
